<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Brazil" title="Climate of Brazil">Climate of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="2617" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-290px-Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-435px-Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-580px-Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif.png 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_climate_classification_Brazil.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brazil map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of Brazil comprises a wide range of weather conditions across a large area and varied topography, but most of the country is tropical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen system</a>, Brazil hosts six major climatic subtypes: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">equatorial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semiarid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">subtropical</a>. The different climatic conditions produce environments ranging from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">equatorial rainforests</a> in the north and semiarid deserts in the northeast, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">temperate coniferous forests</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">tropical savannas</a> in central Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-160">[160]</a></sup> Many regions have starkly different <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BT_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-BT-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>An equatorial climate characterizes much of northern Brazil. There is no real <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, but there are some variations in the period of the year when most rain falls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-160">[160]</a></sup> Temperatures average 25 °C (77 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BT_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-BT-162">[162]</a></sup> with more significant temperature variation between night and day than between seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over central Brazil rainfall is more seasonal, characteristic of a savanna climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_161-2"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-161">[161]</a></sup> This region is as extensive as the Amazon basin but has a very different climate as it lies farther south at a higher altitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-160">[160]</a></sup> In the interior northeast, seasonal rainfall is even more extreme. The semiarid climatic region generally receives less than 800 millimetres (31.5 in) of rain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> most of which generally falls in a period of three to five months of the year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> and occasionally less than this, creating long periods of drought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_161-3"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-161">[161]</a></sup> Brazil's 1877–78 <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Seca" title="Grande Seca">Grande Seca</a></i> (Great Drought), the worst in Brazil's history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> caused approximately half a million deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> A similarly devastating drought occurred in 1915.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>South of Bahia, near the coasts, and more southerly most of the state of São Paulo, the distribution of rainfall changes, with rain falling throughout the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_160-3"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-160">[160]</a></sup> The south enjoys subtropical conditions, with cool winters and average annual temperatures not exceeding 18 °C (64.4 °F);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BT_162-2"><a href="#cite_note-BT-162">[162]</a></sup> winter frosts and <a href="/wiki/Snow_in_Brazil" title="Snow in Brazil">snowfall</a> are not rare in the highest areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_160-4"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_161-4"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-161">[161]</a></sup></p>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182.66666666667px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_environment">Biodiversity and environment</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">Wildlife of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Brazil" title="Deforestation in Brazil">Deforestation in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conservation_in_Brazil" title="Conservation in Brazil">Conservation in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazil's large territory comprises different ecosystems, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, recognized as having the greatest <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a> in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-168">[168]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Forest" title="Atlantic Forest">Atlantic Forest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">Cerrado</a>, sustaining the greatest biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-169">[169]</a></sup> In the south, the <a href="/wiki/Araucaria" title="Araucaria">Araucaria</a> pine forest grows under temperate conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-169">[169]</a></sup> The rich wildlife of Brazil reflects the variety of natural habitats. Scientists estimate that the total number of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">animal species</a> in Brazil could approach four million, mostly invertebrates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_169-2"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amazon_CIAT_(5).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/220px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/330px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/440px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amazon_CIAT_(5).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, the richest and most biodiverse rainforest in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Larger mammals include carnivores <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">pumas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocelot" title="Ocelot">ocelots</a>, rare <a href="/wiki/Bush_dog" title="Bush dog">bush dogs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>, and herbivores <a href="/wiki/Peccary" title="Peccary">peccaries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">tapirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">anteaters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sloth" title="Sloth">sloths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">armadillos</a>. <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">Deer</a> are plentiful in the south, and many species of <a href="/wiki/New_World_monkey" title="New World monkey">New World monkeys</a> are found in the northern <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rain forests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_169-3"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Concern for the environment has grown in response to global interest in environmental issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_11_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_11-171">[171]</a></sup> Brazil's Amazon Basin is home to an extremely diverse array of fish species, including the <a href="/wiki/Red-bellied_piranha" title="Red-bellied piranha">red-bellied piranha</a>. Despite its reputation as a ferocious freshwater fish, the red-bellied piranha is actually a generally timid scavenger. Biodiversity can contribute to <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, livestock, forestry and fisheries extraction. However, almost all economically exploited species of plants, such as soybeans and coffee, or animals, such as chickens, are imported from other countries, and the economic use of native species still crawls. In the Brazilian GDP, the forest sector represents just over 1% and fishing 0.4%.</p>
<p>The natural heritage of Brazil is severely threatened by cattle ranching and agriculture, logging, mining, resettlement, oil and gas extraction, over-fishing, wildlife trade, dams and infrastructure, water pollution, climate change, fire, and invasive species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-168">[168]</a></sup> In many areas of the country, the natural environment is threatened by development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Construction of highways has opened up previously remote areas for agriculture and settlement; dams have flooded valleys and inundated wildlife habitats; and mines have scarred and polluted the landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_11_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_11-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> At least 70 dams are said to be planned for the Amazon region, including the controversial <a href="/wiki/Belo_Monte_Dam" title="Belo Monte Dam">Belo Monte</a> hydroelectric dam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerycaption">Biodiversity of Brazil</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 157.33333333333px">
<div style="width: 157.33333333333px">

</div>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Brazil" title="Politics of Brazil">Politics of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Brazil" title="Federal government of Brazil">Federal government of Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Brazil" title="Elections in Brazil">Elections in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg/330px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg/440px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto_GGFD8938.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a> ("Plateau Palace"), the official workplace of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The form of government is that of a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federative</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The president is both head of state and head of government of the Union and is elected for a four-year term,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> with the possibility of re-election for a second successive term. The current president is <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a>, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> after her <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">impeachment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-175">[175]</a></sup> The President appoints the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State" title="Minister of State">Ministers of State</a>, who assist in government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Legislative houses in each political entity are the main source of law in Brazil. The <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress</a> is the Federation's bicameral legislature, consisting of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Brazil" title="Chamber of Deputies of Brazil">Chamber of Deputies</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_of_Brazil" title="Senate of Brazil">Federal Senate</a>. Judiciary authorities exercise jurisdictional duties almost exclusively. Brazil is a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Brazilian Federation is the "indissoluble union" of the States, the Municipalities and the Federal District.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The Union, the states and the Federal District, and the municipalities, are the "spheres of government". The <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a> is set on five fundamental principles:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> sovereignty, citizenship, dignity of human beings, the social values of labour and freedom of enterprise, and political pluralism. The classic tripartite branches of government (executive, legislative and judicial under a checks and balances system) are formally established by the Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The executive and legislative are organized <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">independently in all three spheres of government</a>, while the judiciary is organized only at the federal and state/Federal District spheres.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1162" data-file-width="2048" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/220px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/330px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/440px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress of Brazil</a>, seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All members of the executive and legislative branches are directly elected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-embassy_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Judges and other judicial officials are appointed after passing entry exams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-embassy_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-177">[177]</a></sup> For most of its democratic history, Brazil has had a multi-party system, proportional representation. Voting is compulsory for the literate between 18 and 70 years old and optional for illiterates and those between 16 and 18 or beyond 70.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-7"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Together with several smaller parties, four political parties stand out: <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_(Brazil)" title="Workers' Party (Brazil)">Workers' Party</a> (PT), <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Social_Democracy_Party" title="Brazilian Social Democracy Party">Brazilian Social Democracy Party</a> (PSDB), <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Democratic_Movement_Party" title="Brazilian Democratic Movement Party">Brazilian Democratic Movement Party</a> (PMDB) and <a href="/wiki/Democrats_(Brazil)" title="Democrats (Brazil)">Democrats</a> (DEM). Fifteen political parties are represented in Congress. It is common for politicians to switch parties, and thus the proportion of congressional seats held by particular parties changes regularly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Almost all governmental and administrative functions are exercised by authorities and agencies affiliated to the Executive.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Brazil" title="Law of Brazil">Law of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Brazil" title="Law enforcement in Brazil">Law enforcement in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Brazil" title="Crime in Brazil">Crime in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazilian law is based on the <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> legal system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> concepts prevail over common law practice. Most of Brazilian law is codified, although non-codified statutes also represent a substantial part, playing a complementary role. Court decisions set out interpretive guidelines; however, they are seldom binding on other specific cases. Doctrinal works and the works of academic jurists have strong influence in law creation and in law cases.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Supremo_Brasil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/220px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/330px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/440px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Supremo_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court_of_Brazil" title="Supreme Federal Court of Brazil">Supreme Federal Court of Brazil</a> serves primarily as the Constitutional Court of the country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The legal system is based on the Federal Constitution, which was promulgated on 5 October 1988, and is the fundamental law of Brazil. All other legislation and court decisions must conform to its rules.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> As of April 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brazil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there have been 53 amendments. States have their own constitutions, which must not contradict the Federal Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Municipalities and the Federal District have "organic laws" (<span lang="pt"><i>leis orgânicas</i></span>), which act in a similar way to constitutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeffentiBarral2011_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeffentiBarral2011-184">[184]</a></sup> Legislative entities are the main source of statutes, although in certain matters judiciary and executive bodies may enact legal norms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-8"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Jurisdiction is administered by the judiciary entities, although in rare situations the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Federal Constitution</a> allows the Federal Senate to pass on legal judgments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-9"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> There are also specialized military, labor, and electoral courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-10"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The highest court is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">Supreme Federal Court</a>.</p>
<p>This system has been criticized over the last few decades for the slow pace of decision-making. Lawsuits on appeal may take several years to resolve, and in some cases more than a decade elapses before definitive rulings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Supreme Federal Tribunal was the first court in the world to transmit its sessions on television, and also via <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> More recently, in December 2009, the Supreme Court adopted <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> to display items on the day planner of the ministers, to inform the daily actions of the Court and the most important decisions made by them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Armed_Forces" title="Brazilian Armed Forces">Brazilian Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="3965" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/220px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/330px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/440px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Brazilian Army</a> participating in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_peacekeeping" title="UN peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The armed forces of Brazil are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">second largest</a> in Latin America by active personnel and the largest in terms of military equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Brazilian Army</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army_Aviation_Command" title="Brazilian Army Aviation Command">Army Aviation Command</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">Brazilian Navy</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Marine_Corps" title="Brazilian Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Naval_Aviation" title="Brazilian Naval Aviation">Naval Aviation</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">Brazilian Air Force</a>. Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> policy gives it one of the world's largest military forces, estimated at more than 1.6 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_Reserve" title="Military Reserve">reservist</a> annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numbering close to 236,000 active personnel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> the Brazilian Army has the largest number of armored vehicles in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, including armored transports and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_tank" title="Battle tank">tanks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-militarypower1_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-militarypower1-192">[192]</a></sup> It is also unique in Latin America for its large, elite forces specializing in unconventional missions, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Special_Operations_Command" title="Brazilian Special Operations Command">Brazilian Special Operations Command</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> and the versatile Strategic Rapid Action Force, made up of highly mobilized and prepared (Special Operations Brigade, <a href="/wiki/Parachute_Infantry_Brigade_(Brazil)" title="Parachute Infantry Brigade (Brazil)">Infantry Brigade Parachutist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> 1st Jungle Infantry Battalion (Airmobile)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> and 12th Brigade Light Infantry (Airmobile)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> able to act anywhere in the country, on short notice, to counter external aggression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The states' <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_(Brazil)" title="Military Police (Brazil)">Military Police</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Military_Firefighters_Corps" title="Military Firefighters Corps">Military Firefighters Corps</a> are described as an ancillary forces of the Army by the constitution, but are under the control of each state's governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-11"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1473" data-file-width="3600" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/330px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/495px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/660px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Various aircraft participate in the <a href="/wiki/South_America_air_forces_maneuvers" title="South America air forces maneuvers">CRUZEX</a> exercise on 11 November 2010, at <a href="/wiki/Natal_Air_Force_Base" title="Natal Air Force Base">Natal Air Force Base</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Navy once operated some of the most powerful warships in the world with the two <a href="/wiki/Minas_Geraes-class_battleship" title="Minas Geraes-class battleship"><i>Minas Geraes</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnoughts</a>, which sparked a <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">South American dreadnought race</a> between Argentina, Brazil, and Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Today, it is a <a href="/wiki/Green-water_navy" title="Green-water navy">green water</a> force and has a group of specialized elite in retaking ships and naval facilities, <a href="/wiki/GRUMEC" title="GRUMEC">GRUMEC</a>, unit specially trained to protect Brazilian oil platforms along its coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> It's the only navy in Latin America that operates an <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(A12)" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier São Paulo (A12)">NAe São Paulo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> and one of the ten navies of the world to operate this type of ship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-militarypower1_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-militarypower1-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Air Force, it is the largest in Latin America has about 700 manned aircraft in service and effective about 67,000 personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil has not been invaded since 1865 during the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> Additionally, Brazil has no contested territorial disputes with any of its neighbours<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> and neither does it have rivalries, like Chile and Bolivia have with each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The Brazilian military has also three times intervened militarily to overthrow the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Brazil" title="Government of Brazil">Brazilian government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revistaepoca.globo.com_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-revistaepoca.globo.com-209">[209]</a></sup> It has built a tradition of participating in UN <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> missions such as in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<center>
<table class="toccolours" style="float:center; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px #ddd solid;">

</center>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Brazil" title="Foreign relations of Brazil">Foreign relations of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Itamaraty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/220px-Itamaraty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/330px-Itamaraty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/440px-Itamaraty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Itamaraty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Itamaraty_Palace" title="Itamaraty Palace">Itamaraty Palace</a>, the seat of <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Brazil)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Brazil)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's international relations are based on Article 4 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Federal Constitution</a>, which establishes <a href="/wiki/Non-interventionism" title="Non-interventionism">non-intervention</a>, <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">international cooperation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peacebuilding" title="Peacebuilding">peaceful settlement of conflicts</a> as the guiding principles of Brazil's relationship with other countries and multilateral organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Constitution, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a> has ultimate authority over foreign policy, while the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">Congress</a> is tasked with reviewing and considering all diplomatic nominations and <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">international treaties</a>, as well as legislation relating to Brazilian foreign policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil's foreign policy is a by-product of the country's unique position as a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, a leader among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>, and an emerging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_power" title="World power">world power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Brazilian foreign policy has generally been based on the principles of <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">multilateralism</a>, peaceful dispute settlement, and non-intervention in the affairs of other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>An increasingly well-developed tool of Brazil's foreign policy is providing aid as a donor to other developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-215">[215]</a></sup> Brazil does not just use its growing economic strength to provide financial aid, but it also provides high levels of expertise and most importantly of all, a quiet non-confrontational diplomacy to improve governance levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-215">[215]</a></sup> Total aid is estimated to be around $1 billion per year that includes:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/330px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/495px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/660px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Brazil" title="List of diplomatic missions in Brazil">Diplomatic missions of Brazil</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>technical cooperation of around $480 million ($30 million in 2010 provided directly by the Brazilian Cooperation Agency (ABC))</li>
<li>an estimated $450 million for in-kind expertise provided by Brazilian institutions specialising in technical cooperation</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, Brazil manages a peacekeeping mission in <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">Haiti</a> ($350 million) and makes in-kind contributions to the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> ($300 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_215-3"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-215">[215]</a></sup> This is in addition to humanitarian assistance and contributions to multilateral development agencies. The scale of this aid places it on par with China and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_215-4"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-215">[215]</a></sup> The Brazilian South-South aid has been described as a "global model in waiting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_crime">Law enforcement and crime</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Brazil" title="Law enforcement in Brazil">Law enforcement in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Brazil" title="Crime in Brazil">Crime in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2309" data-file-width="3603" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/220px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/330px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/440px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Helicopter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" title="Federal Police Department">Federal Police Department</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Brazil, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Constitution</a> establishes five different police agencies for law enforcement: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" title="Federal Police Department">Federal Police Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Highway_Police" title="Federal Highway Police">Federal Highway Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railroad_Police" title="Federal Railroad Police">Federal Railroad Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_(Brazil)" title="Military Police (Brazil)">Military Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_Police_(Brazil)" title="Civil Police (Brazil)">Civil Police</a>. Of these, the first three are affiliated with federal authorities and the last two are subordinate to state governments. All police forces are the responsibility of the executive branch of any of the federal or state powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-12"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Security_Force" title="National Public Security Force">National Public Security Force</a> also can act in public disorder situations arising anywhere in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<p>The country still has above-average levels of violent crime and particularly high levels of gun violence and homicide. In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) estimated the number of 32 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">highest rates of intentional homicide of the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> The number considered tolerable by the WHO is about 10 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> However, there are differences between the crime rates in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">Brazilian states</a>. While in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a> the homicide rate registered in 2013 was 10.8 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants, in <a href="/wiki/Alagoas" title="Alagoas">Alagoas</a> it was 64.7 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil also has high levels of incarceration and the third largest prison population in the world (behind only <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>), with an estimated total of approximately 700,000 prisoners around the country (June 2014), an increase of about 300% compared to the index registered in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> The high number of prisoners eventually overloaded the Brazilian prison system, leading to a shortfall of about two hundred thousand accommodations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>

</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">States of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Brazil" title="Municipalities of Brazil">Municipalities of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Brazil" title="Regions of Brazil">Regions of Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazil is a federation composed of 26 <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">States</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal district</a> (which contains the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">Municipalities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-13"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> States have autonomous administrations, collect their own taxes and receive a share of taxes collected by the Federal government. They have a governor and a unicameral legislative body elected directly by their voters. They also have independent Courts of Law for common justice. Despite this, states have much less autonomy to create their own laws than in the United States. For example, criminal and civil laws can be voted by only the federal bicameral Congress and are uniform throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-14"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The states and the federal district may be grouped into regions: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Region,_Brazil" title="Northern Region, Brazil">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Northeast Region, Brazil">Northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Central-West Region, Brazil">Central-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">Southeast</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Region,_Brazil" title="Southern Region, Brazil">Southern</a>. The Brazilian regions are merely geographical, not political or administrative divisions, and they do not have any specific form of government. Although defined by law, Brazilian regions are useful mainly for statistical purposes, and also to define the distribution of federal funds in development projects.</p>
<p>Municipalities, as the states, have autonomous administrations, collect their own taxes and receive a share of taxes collected by the Union and state government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-15"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Each has a mayor and an elected legislative body, but no separate Court of Law. Indeed, a Court of Law organized by the state can encompass many municipalities in a single justice administrative division called <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a></i> (county).</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Economy of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">Brazilian real</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:443px;max-width:443px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:237px;max-width:237px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1918" data-file-width="3612" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/235px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/353px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/470px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" width="235"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Quotes panel of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">BM&amp;F Bovespa</a>, in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, the country's <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_(15414135738).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1136" data-file-width="1800" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/200px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/300px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/400px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center>A <a href="/wiki/Embraer_KC-390" title="Embraer KC-390">KC-390</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_transport_aircraft" title="Military transport aircraft">military transport aircraft</a>, developed by Brazilian company <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a>, the third largest producer of civil aircraft, after <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil is the largest national economy in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">world's ninth largest economy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">eighth largest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) according to the 2017 estimates. Brazil has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> with abundant natural resources. After rapid growth in preceding decades, the country <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%932016_Brazilian_economic_recession" title="2014–2016 Brazilian economic recession">entered an ongoing recession in 2014</a> amid a political corruption scandal and nationwide protests.</p>
<p>Its GDP (PPP) per capita was $15,048 in 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-imf-224">[224]</a></sup> putting Brazil in the 77th position according to IMF data. Active in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service sectors</a> Brazil has a labor force of over a 107 million (ranking 6th worldwide) and unemployment of 6.2% (ranking 64th worldwide).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Econ_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Econ-225">[225]</a></sup> The country has been expanding its presence in international financial and <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodities markets</a>, and is one of a group of four emerging economies called the <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Brazil has been the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Brazil" title="Coffee production in Brazil">producer of coffee</a> for the last 150 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neilson102_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neilson102-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arroz_097.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1456" data-file-width="2592" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/220px-Arroz_097.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/330px-Arroz_097.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/440px-Arroz_097.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arroz_097.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Combine_harvester" title="Combine harvester">Combine harvester</a> in a rice plantation in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>. Brazil is the third largest exporter of agricultural products in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exporta.C3.A7.C3.A3oagr.C3.ADcola_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-exporta.C3.A7.C3.A3oagr.C3.ADcola-227">[227]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2458" data-file-width="1783" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/220px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/330px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/440px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank of Brazil</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil has become the fourth largest car market in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Major export products include <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">aircraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_equipment" title="Electrical equipment">electrical equipment</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Footwear" title="Footwear">footwear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corned_beef" title="Corned beef">corned beef</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> In total, Brazil ranks 23rd worldwide in <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">value of exports</a>.</p>
<p>Brazil pegged its currency, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">real</a>, to the U.S. dollar in 1994. However, after the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">East Asian financial crisis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">Russian default</a> in 1998<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> and the series of adverse financial events that followed it, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank of Brazil</a> temporarily changed its <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> to a managed-float<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> scheme while undergoing a <a href="/wiki/Currency_crisis" title="Currency crisis">currency crisis</a>, until definitively changing the exchange regime to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free-float" title="Free-float">free-float</a> in January 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil received an International Monetary Fund rescue package in mid-2002 of $30.4 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> then a record sum. Brazil's central bank paid back the IMF loan in 2005, although it was not due to be repaid until 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> One of the issues the Central Bank of Brazil recently dealt with was an excess of speculative short-term capital inflows to the country, which may have contributed to a fall in the value of the U.S. dollar against the real during that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Nonetheless, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> (FDI), related to long-term, less speculative investment in production, is estimated to be $193.8 billion for 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> Inflation monitoring and control currently plays a major part in the Central bank's role of setting out short-term <a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">interest rates</a> as a monetary policy measure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1993 and 2010, 7012 <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers &amp; acquisitions</a> with a total known value of $707 billion with the involvement of Brazilian firms have been announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> The year 2010 was a new record in terms of value with 115 billion USD of transactions. The largest transaction with involvement of Brazilian companies has been: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vale_(mining_company)" title="Vale (mining company)">Cia. Vale do Rio Doce</a> acquired <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vale_Inco" title="Vale Inco">Inco</a> in a tender offer valued at US$18.9 billion.</p>
<p>Corruption costs Brazil almost $41 billion a year alone, with 69.9% of the country's firms identifying the issue as a major constraint in successfully penetrating the global market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Local government corruption is so prevalent that voters perceive it as a problem only if it surpasses certain levels, and only if a local media e.g. a radio station is present to divulge the findings of corruption charges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Initiatives, like this exposure, strengthen awareness which is indicated by the Transparency International's <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>; ranking Brazil 69th out of 178 countries in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power" title="Purchasing power">purchasing power</a> in Brazil is eroded by the so-called <a href="/wiki/Brazil_cost" title="Brazil cost">Brazil cost</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brcost_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-brcost-242">[242]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Components_and_energy">Components and energy</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Brazil" title="Agriculture in Brazil">Agriculture in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Brazil" title="Mining in Brazil">Mining in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industry_in_Brazil" title="Industry in Brazil">Industry in Brazil</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Brazil" title="Energy policy of Brazil">Energy policy of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform_P-51_(Brazil)-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2657" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/220px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/330px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/440px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform_P-51_(Brazil)-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
P-51, an <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil platform</a> of <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's diversified economy includes agriculture, industry, and a wide range of services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BansalPhatak2009_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-BansalPhatak2009-243">[243]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Brazil" title="Agriculture in Brazil">Agriculture</a> and allied sectors like <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> accounted for 5.1% of the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_GDP_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_GDP-244">[244]</a></sup> Brazil is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_producing_countries_of_agricultural_commodities" title="List of largest producing countries of agricultural commodities">largest producer</a> of oranges, coffee, sugar cane, cassava and sisal, soybeans and papayas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luck1998_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luck1998-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Industry_in_Brazil" title="Industry in Brazil">industry</a> – from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemicals</a> to <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durable_good" title="Durable good">consumer durables</a> – accounted for 30.8% of the gross domestic product.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_GDP_244-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_GDP-244">[244]</a></sup> Industry is highly concentrated in metropolitan São Paulo, Rio de Janeiro, <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GiordanoLanzafame2005_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-GiordanoLanzafame2005-246">[246]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_primary_energy_consumption_and_production" title="List of countries by total primary energy consumption and production">tenth largest</a> energy consumer with much of its energy coming from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable sources</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a> is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric plant</a> by energy generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SchmidtOnyango2011_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-SchmidtOnyango2011-247">[247]</a></sup> The first car with an ethanol engine was produced in 1978 and the first airplane engine running on ethanol in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECDDevelopment2001_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECDDevelopment2001-248">[248]</a></sup> Recent oil discoveries in the <a href="/wiki/Pre-salt_layer" title="Pre-salt layer">Pre-salt layer</a> have opened the door for a large increase in oil production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrainardMartinez-Diaz2009_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrainardMartinez-Diaz2009-249">[249]</a></sup> The governmental agencies responsible for the energy policy are the Ministry of Mines and Energy, the National Council for Energy Policy, the <a href="/wiki/National_Agency_of_Petroleum,_Natural_Gas_and_Biofuels_(Brazil)" title="National Agency of Petroleum, Natural Gas and Biofuels (Brazil)">National Agency of Petroleum, Natural Gas and Biofuels</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Electricity_Regulatory_Agency" title="Brazilian Electricity Regulatory Agency">National Agency of Electricity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD2005_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD2005-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1108px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" title="The Itaipu Dam on the Paraná River, located on the border between Brazil and Paraguay, is the second largest of the world (the first is the Three Gorges Dam, in China). Approximately 75% of the Brazilian energy matrix, one of the cleanest in the world, comes from hydropower."><img alt="" data-file-height="651" data-file-width="4016" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/1100px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/1650px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/2200px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg 2x" width="1100"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" title="File:Itaipu à noite.jpg"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná River</a>, located on the border between Brazil and Paraguay, is the second largest of the world (the first is the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges_Dam" title="Three Gorges Dam">Three Gorges Dam</a>, in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>). Approximately 75% of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Brazil" title="Energy policy of Brazil">Brazilian energy matrix</a>, one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clean_energy" title="Clean energy">cleanest</a> in the world, comes from <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brazil" title="Tourism in Brazil">Tourism in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Noronha_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1946" data-file-width="3459" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/220px-Noronha_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/330px-Noronha_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/440px-Noronha_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Noronha_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_Noronha" title="Fernando de Noronha">Fernando de Noronha Archipelago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">Pernambuco</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2836" data-file-width="3781" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg/220px-Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg/330px-Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg/440px-Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cataratas_do_Igua%C3%A7u_-_Vista_de_cima_alt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Iguazu_Falls" title="Iguazu Falls">Iguazu Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Argentina%E2%80%93Brazil_relations" title="Argentina–Brazil relations">Brazil-Argentina border</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism in Brazil is a growing sector and key to the economy of several regions of the country. The country had 6.36 million visitors in 2015, ranking in terms of the international tourist arrivals as the main destination in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and second in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> after <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> Revenues from international tourists reached <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6</span> billion in 2010, showing a recovery from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession">2008–2009 economic crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNWTO2011_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNWTO2011-252">[252]</a></sup> Historical records of 5.4 million visitors and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.8</span> billion in receipts were reached in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MT1_2011_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-MT1_2011-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MT2_2011_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-MT2_2011-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
<p>Natural areas are its most popular tourism product, a combination of <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> with <a href="/wiki/Leisure" title="Leisure">leisure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>, mainly sun and beach, and <a href="/wiki/Adventure_travel" title="Adventure travel">adventure travel</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">cultural tourism</a>. Among the most popular destinations are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beach" title="Beach">beaches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Northeast Region, Brazil">Northeast Region</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pantanal" title="Pantanal">Pantanal</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Center-West Region, Brazil">Center-West Region</a>, beaches at <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>, cultural tourism in <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> and business trips to <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palhares2012_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Palhares2012-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Index</a> (TTCI), which is a measurement of the factors that make it attractive to develop business in the travel and tourism industry of individual countries, Brazil ranked in the 28st place at the world's level, third in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTCI2013_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-TTCI2013-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil's main competitive advantages are its natural resources, which ranked 1st on this criteria out of all countries considered, and ranked 23rd for its cultural resources, due to its many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage sites</a>. The TTCI report notes Brazil's main weaknesses: its ground transport infrastructure remains underdeveloped (ranked 116th), with the quality of roads ranking in 105th place; and the country continues to suffer from a lack of price competitiveness (ranked 114th), due in part to high ticket taxes and airport charges, as well as high prices and high taxation. Safety and security have improved significantly: 75th in 2011, up from 128th in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTCI2013_257-1"><a href="#cite_note-TTCI2013-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> (WTO), international travel to Brazil accelerated in 2000, particularly during 2004 and 2005. However, in 2006 a slow-down took place, and international arrivals had almost no growth in 2007–08.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO2007_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTO2007-258">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMBRATUR09_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMBRATUR09-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abismo_Anhumas,_Bonito,_MS.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG/220px-Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG/330px-Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG/440px-Abismo_Anhumas%2C_Bonito%2C_MS.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abismo_Anhumas,_Bonito,_MS.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bonito,_Mato_Grosso_do_Sul" title="Bonito, Mato Grosso do Sul">Bonito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso_do_Sul" title="Mato Grosso do Sul">Mato Grosso do Sul</a>. The rivers in the region are known for their <a href="/wiki/Crystal" title="Crystal">crystal</a> clear waters.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3571" data-file-width="5357" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg/220px-Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg/330px-Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg/440px-Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_do_Morro_Dona_Marta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The city of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> is featured in <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> in Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In spite of this trend, revenues from international tourism continued to rise, from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">USD</a> 4 billion in 2005 to 5 billion in 2007, despite 330 000 fewer arrivals. This favorable trend is the result of the strong devaluation of the US dollar against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Real" title="Brazilian Real">Brazilian Real</a>, which began in 2004, but which makes Brazil a more expensive international destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boletim0207_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boletim0207-261">[261]</a></sup> This trend changed in 2009, when both visitors and revenues fell as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> of 2008–09.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO2010_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTO2010-262">[262]</a></sup> By 2010, the industry had recovered, and arrivals grew above 2006 levels to 5.2 million international visitors, and receipts from these visitors reached USD 6 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNWTO2011_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNWTO2011-252">[252]</a></sup> In 2011 the historical record was reached with 5.4 million visitors and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.8</span> billion in receipts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MT1_2011_253-1"><a href="#cite_note-MT1_2011-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MT2_2011_254-1"><a href="#cite_note-MT2_2011-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
