<p>Despite continuing record-breaking international tourism revenues, the number of Brazilian tourists travelling overseas has been growing steadily since 2003, resulting in a net negative <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> balance, as more money is spent abroad by Brazilians than comes in as receipts from international tourists visiting Brazil. Tourism expenditures abroad grew from USD 5.8 billion in 2006, to USD 8.2 billion in 2007, a 42% increase, representing a net deficit of USD 3.3 billion in 2007, as compared to USD 1.5 billion in 2006, a 125% increase from the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boletim0308_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boletim0308-263">[263]</a></sup> This trend is caused by Brazilians taking advantage of the stronger <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">Real</a> to travel and making relatively cheaper expenditures abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boletim0308_263-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boletim0308-263">[263]</a></sup> Brazilians traveling overseas in 2006 represented 4% of the country's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIPE006_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIPE006-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, tourism contributed with 3.2% of the country's revenues from exports of goods and services, and represented 7% of direct and indirect employment in the Brazilian economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BID2006_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-BID2006-265">[265]</a></sup> In 2006 direct employment in the sector reached 1.9 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPEA08_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPEA08-266">[266]</a></sup> Domestic tourism is a fundamental market segment for the industry, as 51 million people traveled throughout the country in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIPE007_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIPE007-267">[267]</a></sup> and direct revenues from Brazilian tourists reached USD 22 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> 5.6 times more receipts than international tourists in 2005.</p>
<p>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foz_do_Igua%C3%A7u" title="Foz do Iguaçu">Foz do Iguaçu</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florianópolis">Florianópolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a> were the most visited cities by international tourists for leisure trips. The most popular destinations for business trips were <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMBRATUR06_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMBRATUR06-269">[269]</a></sup> In 2006 Rio de Janeiro and <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a> were the most popular destinations for business trips.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Brazil" title="Science and technology in Brazil">Science and technology in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4518" data-file-width="7360" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg/220px-30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg/330px-30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg/440px-30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:30_Anos_Laborat%C3%B3rio_Sincrotron.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Laborat%C3%B3rio_Nacional_de_Luz_S%C3%ADncrotron" title="Laboratório Nacional de Luz Síncrotron">National Synchrotron Light Laboratory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="State of São Paulo">state of São Paulo</a>, the only <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle accelerator</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vls1-mockup-test.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="620" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Vls1-mockup-test.jpg/220px-Vls1-mockup-test.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Vls1-mockup-test.jpg/330px-Vls1-mockup-test.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Vls1-mockup-test.jpg/440px-Vls1-mockup-test.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vls1-mockup-test.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/VLS-1" title="VLS-1">VLS-1</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A2ntara_Launch_Center" title="Alcântara Launch Center">Alcântara Launch Center</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Space_Agency" title="Brazilian Space Agency">Brazilian Space Agency</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Technological research in Brazil is largely carried out in public universities and research institutes, with the majority of funding for basic research coming from various government agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DevelopmentStaff2006v_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-DevelopmentStaff2006v-270">[270]</a></sup> Brazil's most esteemed technological hubs are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Oswaldo_Cruz" title="Fundação Oswaldo Cruz">Oswaldo Cruz Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Butantan" title="Instituto Butantan">Butantan Institute</a>, the Air Force's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_General_Command_for_Aerospace_Technology" title="Brazilian General Command for Aerospace Technology">Aerospace Technical Center</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empresa_Brasileira_de_Pesquisa_Agropecu%C3%A1ria" title="Empresa Brasileira de Pesquisa Agropecuária">Brazilian Agricultural Research Corporation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Space_Research" title="National Institute for Space Research">INPE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scientific2010f_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scientific2010f-271">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HarveySmid2010_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-HarveySmid2010-272">[272]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Space_Agency" title="Brazilian Space Agency">Brazilian Space Agency</a> has the most advanced space program in Latin America, with significant resources to launch vehicles, and manufacture of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_satellite" title="Artificial satellite">satellite</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrocittiVallance2012.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DvP9jHaoL_s4C.26pg.3DPA628_628.5D_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrocittiVallance2012.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DvP9jHaoL_s4C.26pg.3DPA628_628.5D-273">[273]</a></sup> Owner of relative technological sophistication, the country develops <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, aircraft, as well as being involved in space research, having a Vehicle Launch Center Light and being the only country in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> the integrate team building <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> (ISS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-274">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>The country is also a pioneer in the search for oil in deep water, from where extracts 73% of its reserves. <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">Uranium</a> is enriched at the <a href="/wiki/Resende_Nuclear_Fuel_Factory" title="Resende Nuclear Fuel Factory">Resende Nuclear Fuel Factory</a>, mostly for research purposes (as Brazil obtains 88% from its electricity from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>) and the country's first nuclear submarine will be delivered in 2015 (by France).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> Brazil is one of the three countries in Latin America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> with an operational <a href="/wiki/Synchrotron" title="Synchrotron">Synchrotron</a> Laboratory, a research facility on physics, chemistry, material science and life sciences. And Brazil is the only Latin American country to have a <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductor</a> company with its own <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor_fabrication_plant" title="Semiconductor fabrication plant">fabrication plant</a>, the <a href="/wiki/CEITEC" title="CEITEC">CEITEC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> According to the Global Information Technology Report 2009-2010 of the World Economic Forum, Brazil is the 61 world's largest developer of information technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil also has a large number of outstanding scientific personalities. Among the most renowned Brazilian inventors are priests <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_de_Gusm%C3%A3o" title="Bartolomeu de Gusmão">Bartolomeu de Gusmão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landell_de_Moura" title="Landell de Moura">Landell de Moura</a> and Francisco João de Azevedo, besides <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Santos-Dumont" title="Alberto Santos-Dumont">Alberto Santos-Dumont</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Evaristo_Conrado_Engelberg" title="Evaristo Conrado Engelberg">Evaristo Conrado Engelberg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patentbritish_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-patentbritish-281">[281]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manuel_Dias_de_Abreu" title="Manuel Dias de Abreu">Manuel Dias de Abreu</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Pavel" title="Andreas Pavel">Andreas Pavel</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> e Nélio José Nicolai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Brazilian science is represented by the likes of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Lattes" title="César Lattes">César Lattes</a> (Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a> Pathfinder of <i><a href="/wiki/Pion" title="Pion">Pi Meson</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lattes_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lattes-285">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Schenberg" title="Mário Schenberg">Mário Schenberg</a> (considered the greatest theoretical physicist of Brazil),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Leite_Lopes" title="José Leite Lopes">José Leite Lopes</a> (only Brazilian physicist holder of <i>UNESCO Science Prize</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artur_%C3%81vila" title="Artur Ávila">Artur Ávila</a> (the first Latin American winner of <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_M%C3%BCller" title="Fritz Müller">Fritz Müller</a> (pioneer in factual support the theory of evolution by Charles Darwin).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West.2C_David_A_2003_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-West.2C_David_A_2003-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3194" data-file-width="5022" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/220px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/330px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/440px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminal 3 of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Brazil" title="List of the busiest airports in Brazil">busiest airport in the country</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1023" data-file-width="1065" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg/220px-BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg/330px-BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg/440px-BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BR116_Viaduto_em_Fortaleza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/BR-116" title="BR-116">BR-116</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cear%C3%A1" title="Ceará">Ceará</a>, the longest <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Highway_System" title="Brazilian Highway System">highway</a> in the country, with 4,385 km (2,725 mi) of extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_Santos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Port_Santos.jpg/220px-Port_Santos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Port_Santos.jpg/330px-Port_Santos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Port_Santos.jpg/440px-Port_Santos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_Santos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">Port of Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a>, the busiest port in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brazil" title="Transport in Brazil">Transport in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazilian roads are the primary carriers of freight and passenger traffic. The road system totaled 1.98 million km (1.23 million mi) in 2002. The total of paved roads increased from 35,496 km (22,056 mi) (22,056 mi) in 1967 to 184,140 km (114,419 mi) (114,425 mi) in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first investments in road infrastructure have given up in the 1920s, the government of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Luis" title="Washington Luis">Washington Luis</a>, being pursued in the governments of <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getúlio Vargas">Getúlio Vargas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurico_Gaspar_Dutra" title="Eurico Gaspar Dutra">Eurico Gaspar Dutra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek" title="Juscelino Kubitschek">Juscelino Kubitschek</a> (1956–61), who designed and built the capital <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, was another supporter of highways. Kubitschek was responsible for the installation of major car manufacturers in the country (<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> arrived in Brazil during his rule) and one of the points used to attract them was, of course, support for the construction of highways. With the implementation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> in 1976 ending an automobile market closed loop, from the end of the 1990s the country has received large foreign direct investments installing in its territory other major car manufacturers and utilities, such as <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citroen" title="Citroen">Citroen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> Brazil is the seventh most important country in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auto_industry" title="Auto industry">auto industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">railway</a> system has been declining since 1945, when emphasis shifted to <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highway</a> construction. The total length of railway track was 30,875 km (19,185 mi) in 2002, as compared with 31,848 km (19,789 mi) in 1970. Most of the railway system belonged to the Federal Railroad Corporation RFFSA, which was privatized in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a> was the first underground transit system in Brazil. The other metro systems are in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teresina" title="Teresina">Teresina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>.</p>
<p>The country has an extensive rail network of 28,538 kilometres (17,733 miles) in length, the tenth largest network in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012ciagini_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012ciagini-297">[297]</a></sup> Currently, the Brazilian government, unlike the past, seeks to encourage this mode of transport; an example of this incentive is the project of the <a href="/wiki/Rio%E2%80%93S%C3%A3o_Paulo_high-speed_rail" title="Rio–São Paulo high-speed rail">Rio–São Paulo high-speed rail</a>, that will connect the two main cities of the country to carry passengers.</p>
<p>There are about 2,500 <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airports</a> in Brazil, including landing fields: the second largest number in the world, after the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo-Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo-Guarulhos International Airport</a>, near São Paulo, is the largest and busiest airport with nearly 20 million passengers annually, while handling the vast majority of commercial traffic for the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palhares2012x_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-Palhares2012x-299">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>For freight transport <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterways" title="Waterways">waterways</a> are of importance, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Free_Economic_Zone_of_Manaus" title="Free Economic Zone of Manaus">industrial zones of Manaus</a> can be reached only by means of the Solimões- Amazonas waterway (3,250 kilometres (2,020 miles) with 6 metres (20 feet) minimum depth). The country also has 50,000 kilometres (31,000 miles) of waterways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012ciagini_297-1"><a href="#cite_note-2012ciagini-297">[297]</a></sup></p>
<p>Coastal shipping links widely separated parts of the country. Bolivia and Paraguay have been given free <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ports</a> at <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos</a>. Of the 36 deep-water ports, Santos, Itajaí, Rio Grande, Paranaguá, Rio de Janeiro, Sepetiba, Vitória, Suape, Manaus and São Francisco do Sul are the most important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> Bulk carriers have to wait up to 18 days before being serviced, container ships 36,3 hours on average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Brazil" title="Water supply and sanitation in Brazil">Water supply and sanitation in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG/220px-ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG/330px-ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG/440px-ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ETE_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Tratamento_de_Esgoto_-_Una%C3%AD.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_treatment_plant" title="Water treatment plant">Water treatment plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Una%C3%AD" title="Unaí">Unaí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the achievements in the water supply and sanitation sector is an increase in access to water piped on premises from 79% to 92% between 1990 and 2010; an increase in access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">Improved sanitation</a> from 68% to 79% in the same period;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP2008_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMP2008-302">[302]</a></sup> a functioning national system to finance water and sanitation infrastructure; a high level of cost recovery compared to most other developing countries; as well as a number of notable technical and financial innovations such as <a href="/wiki/Condominial_sewerage" title="Condominial sewerage">Condominial sewerage</a> and an output-based subsidy for treated wastewater called <a href="/wiki/PRODES" title="PRODES">PRODES</a>.</p>
<p>Among the challenges is the still high number of poor Brazilians living in urban slums (<a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">Favela</a>) and in rural areas without access to piped water or sanitation; <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a> in the Northeast of Brazil; <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, especially in the South-East of the country; the low share of collected <a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">wastewater</a> that is being treated (35% in 2000); and long-standing tensions between the federal, state and municipal governments about their respective roles in the sector.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Brazil" title="Health in Brazil">Health in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="850" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/220px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/330px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg/440px-Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Albert_Einstein.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_Hospital" title="Albert Einstein Hospital">Albert Einstein Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> is one of the most well-known health units in Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> system, the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_%C3%9Anico_de_Sa%C3%BAde" title="Sistema Único de Saúde">Unified Health System</a> (SUS), is managed and provided by all levels of government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ForgiaCouttolenc2008_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-ForgiaCouttolenc2008-303">[303]</a></sup> being the largest type system in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Private_healthcare" title="Private healthcare">private healthcare</a> systems play a complementary role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolper2004_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolper2004-305">[305]</a></sup> Public health services are universal and offered to all citizens of the country for free. However, the construction and maintenance of health centers and hospitals are financed by taxes, and the country spends about 9% of its GDP on expenditures in the area. In 2009, the Brazilian territory had 1.72 doctors and 2.4 hospital beds for every 1,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-306">[306]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite all the progress made since the creation of the universal health care system in 1988, there are still several public health problems in Brazil. In 2006, the main points to be solved were the high <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_infant_mortality_rate" title="List of countries by infant mortality rate">infant</a> (2.51%) and maternal mortality rates (73.1 deaths per 1000 births). The number of deaths from noncommunicable diseases, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_diseases" title="Cardiovascular diseases">cardiovascular diseases</a> (151.7 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants) and <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> (72.7 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants), also has a considerable impact on the health of the Brazilian population. Finally, external but preventable factors such as car accidents, violence and suicide caused 14.9% of all deaths in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> The Brazilian health system was ranked 125th among the 191 countries evaluated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Brazil" title="Education in Brazil">Education in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg/220px-Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg/330px-Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg/440px-Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sala_de_aula_CB_Unicamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Classroom in the main campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Campinas" title="University of Campinas">University of Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">Federal Constitution</a> and the Law of Guidelines and Bases of National Education determine that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Government" title="Federal Government">Federal Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_District" title="Federal District">Federal District</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities" title="Municipalities">municipalities</a> must manage and organize their respective education systems. Each of these public educational systems is responsible for its own maintenance, which manages funds as well as the mechanisms and funding sources. The constitution reserves 25% of the state budget and 18% of federal taxes and municipal taxes for education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Usa2005_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-Usa2005-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">IBGE</a>, in 2011, the literacy rate of the population was 90.4%, meaning that 13 million (9.6% of population) people are still illiterate in the country; functional illiteracy has reached 21.6% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agency2010_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-Agency2010-310">[310]</a></sup> Illiteracy is highest in the Northeast, where 19.9% of the population is illiterate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bank2001_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bank2001-311">[311]</a></sup></p>
<p>Higher education starts with undergraduate or sequential <a href="/wiki/Course_(education)" title="Course (education)">courses</a>, which may offer different options of specialization in academic or professional careers. Depending on the choice, students can improve their educational background with courses of post-graduate studies or broad sense. To attend a higher education institution is required, by Law of Guidelines and Bases of Education, completing all levels of education suited to the needs of all students of teaching <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elementary_school" title="Elementary school">elementary</a> and medium, provided the student does not hold any disability, whether physical, <a href="/wiki/Mind" title="Mind">mental</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual" title="Visual">visual</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearing_(sense)" title="Hearing (sense)">hearing</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo</a> is the best <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, according to <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>. Of the top 20 Latin Americans universities, eight are Brazilian. Most of them are <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communication">Media and communication<span id="Media"></span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Brazil" title="Telecommunications in Brazil">Telecommunications in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_ownership_in_Brazil" title="Media ownership in Brazil">Media ownership in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg/220px-Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg/330px-Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg/440px-Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jornal_Nacional_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> at <i><a href="/wiki/Jornal_Nacional" title="Jornal Nacional">Jornal Nacional</a></i> news program. <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a> is the second largest commercial television network of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Brazilian press has its beginnings in 1808 with the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza#Realm_in_Brazil" title="House of Braganza">Portuguese royal family</a> to Brazil, hitherto forbidden any activity of the press – was the publication of newspapers or books. The Brazilian press was officially born in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> on 13 May 1808, with the creation of the Royal Printing, National Press by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" title="Prince Regent">Prince Regent</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" title="João VI of Portugal">Dom João</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Echevarr.C3.ADaPupo-Walker1996_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-Echevarr.C3.ADaPupo-Walker1996-314">[314]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Gazeta do Rio de Janeiro</i>, the first newspaper published in the country, began to circulate on 10 September 1808.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnston2003_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston2003-315">[315]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_the_world_by_circulation" title="List of newspapers in the world by circulation">largest newspapers</a> nowadays are <i><a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S.Paulo" title="Folha de S.Paulo">Folha de S.Paulo</a></i> (from the state of São Paulo), <i>Super Notícia</i> (Minas Gerais 296.799), <i><a href="/wiki/O_Globo" title="O Globo">O Globo</a></i> (RJ 277.876) and <i><a href="/wiki/O_Estado_de_S._Paulo" title="O Estado de S. Paulo">O Estado de S. Paulo</a></i> (SP 235.217).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vincent2003B_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent2003B-316">[316]</a></sup></p>
<p>Radio broadcasting began on 7 September 1922, with a speech by then President Pessoa, and was formalized on 20 April 1923 with the creation of "Radio Society of Rio de Janeiro."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCann2004_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCann2004-317">[317]</a></sup></p>
<p>Television in Brazil began officially on 18 September 1950, with the founding of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV_Tupi" title="TV Tupi">TV Tupi</a> by <a href="/wiki/Assis_Chateaubriand" title="Assis Chateaubriand">Assis Chateaubriand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward2007_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ward2007-318">[318]</a></sup> Since then television has grown in the country, creating large public networks such as Globo, SBT, Record and Bandeirantes. Today it is the most important factor in popular culture of Brazilian society, indicated by research showing that as much as 67%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> of the general population follow the same daily <a href="/wiki/Soap_opera" title="Soap opera">soap opera</a> broadcast. Digital Television, using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SBTVD" title="SBTVD">SBTVD</a> standard (based on the Japanese standard <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISDB-T" title="ISDB-T">ISDB-T</a>), was adopted 29 June 2006 and launched on 2 November 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alencar2009_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alencar2009-321">[321]</a></sup> In May 2010, Brazil launched <a href="/wiki/TV_Brasil_Internacional" title="TV Brasil Internacional">TV Brasil Internacional</a>, an international <a href="/wiki/Television_station" title="Television station">television station</a>, initially broadcasting to 49 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brazil" title="Demographics of Brazil">Demographics of Brazil</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" title="Brazilian people">Brazilian people</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">Immigration to Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_states_by_population_density" title="List of Brazilian states by population density">List of Brazilian states by population density</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="593" height="305" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png/300px-ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png/450px-ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ARCHELLA_E_THERY_Img_05.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population density of Brazilian municipalities.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The population of Brazil, as recorded by the 2008 PNAD, was approximately 190 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> (22.31 inhabitants per square kilometre or 57.8/sq mi), with a ratio of men to women of 0.95:1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> and 83.75% of the population defined as urban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> The population is heavily concentrated in the Southeastern (79.8 million inhabitants) and Northeastern (53.5 million inhabitants) regions, while the two most extensive regions, the Center-West and the North, which together make up 64.12% of the Brazilian territory, have a total of only 29.1 million inhabitants.</p>
<p>The first census in Brazil was carried out in 1872 and recorded a population of 9,930,478.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> From 1880 to 1930, 4 million Europeans arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> Brazil's population increased significantly between 1940 and 1970, because of a decline in the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a>, even though the <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> underwent a slight decline. In the 1940s the annual <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth rate</a> was 2.4%, rising to 3.0% in the 1950s and remaining at 2.9% in the 1960s, as life expectancy rose from 44 to 54 years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> and to 72.6 years in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> It has been steadily falling since the 1960s, from 3.04% per year between 1950 and 1960 to 1.05% in 2008 and is expected to fall to a negative value of –0.29% by 2050<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> thus completing the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">demographic transition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, the illiteracy rate was 11.48%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> and among the <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_Brazil" title="Youth in Brazil">youth</a> (ages 15–19) 1.74%. It was highest (20.30%) in the Northeast, which had a large proportion of rural poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> Illiteracy was high (24.18%) among the rural population and lower (9.05%) among the urban population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_and_ethnicity">Race and ethnicity</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_Brazil" title="Race and ethnicity in Brazil">Race and ethnicity in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/220px-Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/330px-Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG/440px-Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fachada_do_Museu_da_Imigra%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Museum of Immigration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="State of São Paulo">State of São Paulo</a> in the neighborhood of <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Mooca" title="Mooca">Mooca</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_city" title="São Paulo city">São Paulo city</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">National Research by Household Sample</a> (PNAD) of 2008, 48.43% of the population (about 92 million) described themselves as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" title="White Brazilian">White</a>; 43.80% (about 83 million) as <a href="/wiki/Brown_(racial_classification)#Pardos_in_Brazil" title="Brown (racial classification)">Pardo</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_people" title="Brown people">brown</a>), 6.84% (about 13 million) as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Brazilian" title="Black Brazilian">Black</a>; 0.58% (about 1.1 million) as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian</a>; and 0.28% (about 536 thousand) as <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Amerindian</a> (officially called <i>indígena</i>, Indigenous), while 0.07% (about 130 thousand) did not declare their race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNADIBGE_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-PNADIBGE-335">[335]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Nacional_do_%C3%8Dndio" title="Fundação Nacional do Índio">National Indian Foundation</a> estimated that Brazil has 67 different uncontacted tribes, up from their estimate of 40 in 2005. Brazil is believed to have the largest number of <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted peoples</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the arrival of the Portuguese in 1500, considerable <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">miscegenation</a> between Amerindians, Europeans, and Africans has taken place in all regions of the country (with European ancestry being dominant nationwide according to the vast majority of all autosomal studies undertaken covering the entire population, accounting for between 65% to 77%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alvaro.com.br_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-alvaro.com.br-337">[337]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.folha.uol.com.br_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-www1.folha.uol.com.br-338">[338]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bdtd.bce.unb.br_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-bdtd.bce.unb.br-339">[339]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plosone.org_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-plosone.org-340">[340]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p><a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_Brazil" title="Race and ethnicity in Brazil">Race and ethnicity in Brazil</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBGE_Censo_de_2000_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBGE_Censo_de_2000-341">[341]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Etnias_Censo_2010_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-Etnias_Censo_2010-342">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:LightBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" title="White Brazilian">White</a> (47.7%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #9966CC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pardo_Brazilian" title="Pardo Brazilian">Pardo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Multiracial#Brazil" title="Multiracial">Multiracial</a>) (43.1%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumAquamarine; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Brazilian" title="Black Brazilian">Black</a> (7.6%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFE135; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian</a> (1.1%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Natives</a> (0.4%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazilian society is more <a href="/wiki/Social_issues_in_Brazil" title="Social issues in Brazil">markedly divided by social class lines</a>, although a high <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality_in_Brazil" title="Income inequality in Brazil">income disparity</a> is found <a href="/wiki/Social_apartheid_in_Brazil" title="Social apartheid in Brazil">between race groups</a>, so <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Class_discrimination" title="Class discrimination">classism</a> can be conflated. Socially significant closeness to one racial group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_in_Brazil" title="Race in Brazil">is taken in account</a> more in the basis of appearance (<a href="/wiki/Phenotype" title="Phenotype">phenotypes</a>) rather than ancestry, to the extent that full <a href="/wiki/Sibling" title="Sibling">siblings</a> can pertain to different "racial" groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_status" title="Socioeconomic status">Socioeconomic</a> factors are also significant, because a minority of <i><a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">pardos</a></i> are likely to start declaring themselves White or Black if socially upward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> Skin color and facial features do not line quite well with ancestry (usually, Afro-Brazilians are evenly mixed and European ancestry is dominant in Whites and <i>pardos</i> with a significant non-European contribution, but the individual variation is great).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plosone.org_340-1"><a href="#cite_note-plosone.org-340">[340]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afrobras_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-afrobras-346">[346]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup></p>
<p>The brown population (officially called <i><a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">pardo</a></i> in Portuguese, also colloquially <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/moreno" title="wikt:moreno">moreno</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coelho_1996.2C_p..C2.A0268_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coelho_1996.2C_p..C2.A0268-349">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vesentini_1988.2C_p..C2.A0117_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vesentini_1988.2C_p..C2.A0117-350">[350]</a></sup> is a broad category that includes <i><a href="/wiki/Caboclo" title="Caboclo">caboclos</a></i> (assimilated Amerindians in general, and descendants of Whites and Natives), <i><a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulatos</a></i> (descendants of primarily Whites and Afro-Brazilians) and <i><a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">cafuzos</a></i> (descendants of Afro-Brazilians and Natives).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coelho_1996.2C_p..C2.A0268_349-1"><a href="#cite_note-Coelho_1996.2C_p..C2.A0268-349">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vesentini_1988.2C_p..C2.A0117_350-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vesentini_1988.2C_p..C2.A0117-350">[350]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108-353">[353]</a></sup> People of considerable Amerindian ancestry form the majority of the population in the Northern, Northeastern and Center-Western regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup></p>
<p>Higher percents of Blacks, mulattoes and tri-racials can be found in the eastern coast of the Northeastern region from Bahia to Paraíba<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108_353-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108-353">[353]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup> and also in northern Maranhão,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-357"><a href="#cite_note-357">[357]</a></sup> southern Minas Gerais<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Azevedo_1971.2C_p..C2.A0161_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-Azevedo_1971.2C_p..C2.A0161-358">[358]</a></sup> and in eastern Rio de Janeiro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108_353-2"><a href="#cite_note-Moreira_1981.2C_p..C2.A0108-353">[353]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Azevedo_1971.2C_p..C2.A0161_358-1"><a href="#cite_note-Azevedo_1971.2C_p..C2.A0161-358">[358]</a></sup> From the 19th century, Brazil opened its borders to <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">immigration</a>. About five million people from over 60 countries migrated to Brazil between 1808 and 1972, most of them of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilians_of_Spanish_descent" title="Brazilians of Spanish descent">Spanish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Brazilian" title="German Brazilian">German</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Brazilian" title="Ukrainian Brazilian">Ukrainian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_Brazilian" title="Polish Brazilian">Polish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Brazilian" title="Jewish Brazilian">Jewish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russians_in_Brazil" title="Russians in Brazil">Russian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Brazilian" title="Chinese Brazilian">Chinese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" title="Arab Brazilian">Arab</a> origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Brazil" title="Religion in Brazil">Religion in Brazil</a></div>

</div>
<p>Religion in Brazil formed from the meeting of the Catholic Church with the religious traditions of enslaved African peoples and indigenous peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoyleSheen2013_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoyleSheen2013-361">[361]</a></sup> This confluence of faiths during the Portuguese colonization of Brazil led to the development of a diverse array of syncretistic practices within the overarching umbrella of Brazilian Catholic Church, characterized by traditional Portuguese festivities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-georgetown1_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-georgetown1-362">[362]</a></sup> and in some instances, <a href="/wiki/Allan_Kardec" title="Allan Kardec">Allan Kardec</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">Spiritism</a> (a religion which incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">spiritualism</a> and Christianity). Religious pluralism increased during the 20th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris2006a_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morris2006a-363">[363]</a></sup> and the Protestant community has grown to include over 22% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JeynesRobinson2012_364-0"><a href="#cite_note-JeynesRobinson2012-364">[364]</a></sup> The most common Protestant denominations are <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> ones. Other Protestant branches with a notable presence in the country include the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Reformed tradition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:212px;max-width:212px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida,_2007.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1611" data-file-width="2480" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg/210px-Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg/315px-Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg/420px-Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida%2C_2007.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Aparecida" title="Basilica of the National Shrine of Our Lady of Aparecida">Basilica of the National Shrine of Our Lady of Aparecida</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aparecida_do_Norte" title="Aparecida do Norte">Aparecida do Norte</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a>, is the second largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Brazil" title="Roman Catholicism in Brazil">Catholic</a> church in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-366"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> is the country's predominant faith. Brazil has the world's largest Catholic population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDS_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDS-369">[369]</a></sup> According to the 2000 Demographic Census (the PNAD survey does not inquire about religion), 73.57% of the population followed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Brazil" title="Roman Catholicism in Brazil">Roman Catholicism</a>; 15.41% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Brazil" title="Protestantism in Brazil">Protestantism</a>; 1.33% Kardecist spiritism; 1.22% other Christian denominations; 0.31% Afro-Brazilian religions; 0.13% <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>; 0.05% <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>; 0.02% <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Brazil" title="Islam in Brazil">Islam</a>; 0.01% Amerindian religions; 0.59% other religions, undeclared or undetermined; while 7.35% have no religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Censo2000Religiao_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-Censo2000Religiao-370">[370]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, in the last ten years Protestantism, particularly Pentecostalism and Evangelicalism, has spread in Brazil, while the proportion of Catholics has dropped significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-georgetown2_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-georgetown2-371">[371]</a></sup> After Protestantism, individuals professing no religion are also a significant group, exceeding 7% of the population as of the 2000 census. The cities of <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Roraima" title="Boa Vista, Roraima">Boa Vista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Velho" title="Porto Velho">Porto Velho</a> have the greatest proportion of <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Irreligious</a> residents in Brazil. <a href="/wiki/Teresina" title="Teresina">Teresina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florianópolis">Florianópolis</a> were the most Roman Catholic in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FGV_no_G1_372-0"><a href="#cite_note-FGV_no_G1-372">[372]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Greater Rio de Janeiro">Greater Rio de Janeiro</a>, not including the <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">city proper</a>, is the most irreligious and least Roman Catholic Brazilian periphery, while <a href="/wiki/Greater_Porto_Alegre" title="Greater Porto Alegre">Greater Porto Alegre</a> and Greater <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a> are on the opposite sides of the lists, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FGV_no_G1_372-1"><a href="#cite_note-FGV_no_G1-372">[372]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_in_Brazil" title="List of largest cities in Brazil">List of largest cities in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Brazil" title="Municipalities of Brazil">Municipalities of Brazil</a></div>
<p>According to IBGE (Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics) urban areas already concentrate 84.35% of the population, while the Southeast region remains the most populated one, with over 80 million inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> The largest urban agglomerations in Brazil are <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a> – all in the Southeastern Region – with 21.1, 12.3, and 5.1 million inhabitants respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concentra.C3.A7.C3.B5es_urbanas_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-concentra.C3.A7.C3.B5es_urbanas-374">[374]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-376"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> The majority of state capitals are the largest cities in their states, except for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vit%C3%B3ria,_Brazil" title="Vitória, Brazil">Vitória</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Espírito Santo">Espírito Santo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florianópolis">Florianópolis</a>, the capital of Santa Catarina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Brazil" title="Languages of Brazil">Languages of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian Portuguese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_endangered_languages_in_Brazil" title="List of endangered languages in Brazil">List of endangered languages in Brazil</a></div>
